	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Denis Law</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

<p><b>Denis Law</b> <span class="noexcerpt" style="font-size:100%;"><a href="/wiki/Commander_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander of the Order of the British Empire">CBE</a></span> (born 24 February 1940) is a Scottish former <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who played as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)" title="Forward (association football)">forward</a>. His career as a football player began at Second Division <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Town_A.F.C." title="Huddersfield Town A.F.C.">Huddersfield Town</a> in 1956. After four years at Huddersfield, he was signed by <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> for an estimated transfer fee of £55,000, which set a new British record. Law spent one year there before <a href="/wiki/Torino_Calcio" class="mw-redirect" title="Torino Calcio">Torino</a> bought him for £110,000, this time setting a new record fee for a transfer involving a British player. Although he played well in Italy, he found it difficult to settle there and signed for <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> in 1962, setting another British record transfer fee of £115,000.
</p><p>Law spent 11 years at Manchester United, where he scored 237 goals in 404 appearances. His goals tally places him third in the club's history, behind <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Rooney" title="Wayne Rooney">Wayne Rooney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Charlton" title="Bobby Charlton">Bobby Charlton</a>. He was nicknamed <i>The King</i><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> and <i>The Lawman</i> by supporters, and <i>Denis the Menace</i> by opposing supporters. He is the only Scottish player to have won the <a href="/wiki/Ballon_d%27Or_(1956%E2%80%932009)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ballon d&#39;Or (1956–2009)">Ballon d'Or</a> award, doing so in 1964, and helped his club win the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">First Division</a> in 1965 and 1967. He missed their <a href="/wiki/European_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="European Cup">European Cup</a> triumph in 1968 through injury.
</p><p>Law left Manchester United in 1973 to return to Manchester City for a season, and represented <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scotland</a> at the <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1974 FIFA World Cup">1974 FIFA World Cup</a>. He retired at the start of the 1974–75 season. Law played for Scotland a total of 55 times and jointly holds the Scottish international record goal tally with 30 goals. Law holds a United record for scoring 46 competitive goals in a single season.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denis_Law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Law was born in <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen" title="Aberdeen">Aberdeen</a>, Scotland,<sup id="cite_ref-Hugman_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hugman-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> to George Law, a fisherman, and his wife, Robina; he was the youngest of seven children, four boys and three girls. The Law family were not well off and lived in a council tenement flat at Printfield Terrace in Aberdeen.<sup id="cite_ref-book_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> He went barefoot until he was 12 years old and wore handed-down shoes throughout his adolescence; his first pair of football boots came as a second-hand birthday present from a neighbour, which he received as a teenager.<sup id="cite_ref-book_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He supported <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_F.C." title="Aberdeen F.C.">Aberdeen</a> and watched them when he had enough money to do so, watching local non-league teams when he did not.<sup id="cite_ref-book_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> His obsession with football led to him turning down a place at <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_Grammar_School" title="Aberdeen Grammar School">Aberdeen Grammar School</a>, because he would have had to play rugby there. Instead, he attended <a href="/wiki/St_Machar_Academy" title="St Machar Academy">Powis Academy</a> in Aberdeen. Despite having a serious <a href="/wiki/Strabismus" title="Strabismus">squint</a>, he showed great promise once he was moved from full back to inside-left, and was selected for Scotland Schoolboys.<sup id="cite_ref-book_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denis_Law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Club career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Huddersfield_Town">Huddersfield Town</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denis_Law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Huddersfield Town">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/1954%E2%80%9355_in_English_football" title="1954–55 in English football">1954–55 season</a>, he was spotted by Archie Beattie, a scout for <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Town_A.F.C." title="Huddersfield Town A.F.C.">Huddersfield Town</a>, who invited 14 year-old Law to go for a trial. When he got there, the manager said, "The boy's a freak. Never did I see a less likely football prospect – weak, puny and bespectacled." However, to Law's surprise, they signed him on 3 April 1955. While he was at Huddersfield, he had an operation to correct his squint, which greatly enhanced his self-confidence.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Huddersfield's relegation to what was then the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Second_Division" title="Football League Second Division">Second Division</a> made it easier for Law to get a game, and he made his debut on 24 December 1956, aged only sixteen, in a 2–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Notts_County_F.C." title="Notts County F.C.">Notts County</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Manchester United's manager <a href="/wiki/Matt_Busby" title="Matt Busby">Matt Busby</a> shortly offered Huddersfield £10,000 for Law, a substantial amount of money for a teenage footballer at that time, but the club turned the offer down. <a href="/wiki/Bill_Shankly" title="Bill Shankly">Bill Shankly</a> was manager of Huddersfield between 1957 and 1959, and when he left for <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> he wanted to take Law with him, but Liverpool were unable to afford him at that time.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manchester_City">Manchester City</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denis_Law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Manchester City">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In March 1960, Law signed for <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> for what was then a British record transfer fee, estimated to be £55,000,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;note 1&#93;</a></sup> although Law's share of the fee was "precisely nothing".<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Once again, Matt Busby had attempted to sign Law for Manchester United, but United's <a href="/wiki/Manchester_derby" title="Manchester derby">cross-city rivals</a> beat them to Law's signature.<sup id="cite_ref-book_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>City had narrowly avoided relegation from Division I the previous season, and Law genuinely felt that Huddersfield had a better team at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> He made his debut on 19 March, and scored in a 4–3 defeat to <a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United</a>. In April 1961, he scored two goals in a 4–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a> that ensured City's survival in Division One.
</p><p>Although he had thought about leaving,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> he was playing well and in 1961 Law scored an incredible six goals in an <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> tie against <a href="/wiki/Luton_Town_F.C." title="Luton Town F.C.">Luton Town</a>. Unfortunately for him, the match was abandoned with twenty minutes to go, so his six goals didn't count. To make matters worse for him, Luton won the replay 3–1, and City were knocked out of the Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although he enjoyed his time at City,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> he wanted to play in a more successful side and was sold to the Italian club <a href="/wiki/Torino_Calcio" class="mw-redirect" title="Torino Calcio">Torino</a> in the summer of 1961.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Torino">Torino</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denis_Law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Torino">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Law moved to Torino for a fee of £110,000,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;note 2&#93;</a></sup> (a record fee for a transfer involving a British player)<sup id="cite_ref-torcar_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-torcar-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> and was accompanied by <a href="/wiki/Joe_Baker" title="Joe Baker">Joe Baker</a> who had signed from Scottish side <a href="/wiki/Hibernian_F.C." title="Hibernian F.C.">Hibernian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tor_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tor-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Law's time in Italy did not go according to plan. Another Italian club, <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Internazionale</a>, tried to prevent him becoming a Torino player as soon as he arrived, claiming he had signed a pre-contract agreement with them, although they dropped this claim before the season started.<sup id="cite_ref-book_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tor_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tor-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Players in the UK were not treated well at the time, and the <a href="/wiki/Maximum_wage" title="Maximum wage">maximum wage</a> for footballers had only recently been abolished there, so he was pleasantly surprised to find that pre-season training was based in a luxury hotel in the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-book_4-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> However, Torino took <a href="/wiki/Performance-related_pay" title="Performance-related pay">performance-related pay</a> to something of an extreme, giving the players bags full of money when the team won but little, if anything, when they lost.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Like many British footballers who have gone to play in Italy, Law did not like the style of football and found adapting to it difficult. The ultra-defensive <i><a href="/wiki/Catenaccio" title="Catenaccio">catenaccio</a></i> system was popular there at the time, so forwards did not get many chances to score.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 7 February 1962, he was injured in a car crash when his teammate Joe Baker drove the wrong way around a <a href="/wiki/Roundabout" title="Roundabout">roundabout</a> and clipped the kerb as he tried to turn the car around, flipping it over. Baker was almost killed, but Law's injuries were not life-threatening.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By April, he had put in a transfer request, which was ignored.<sup id="cite_ref-tor_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tor-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The final straw for Law came in a match against <a href="/wiki/SSC_Napoli" class="mw-redirect" title="SSC Napoli">Napoli</a> when he was sent off. After the match, he was told that Torino's coach, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Beniamino_Santos&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Beniamino Santos (page does not exist)">Beniamino Santos</a>, had instructed the referee to send him off because he was angry at Law for taking a throw in, which he had been told not to do.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Law walked out, and was told that he would be transferred to Manchester United. A few days later, however, he was told that he was being sold to <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> and that the <a href="/wiki/Small_print" class="mw-redirect" title="Small print">small print</a> in his contract committed him to going there whether he wanted to or not. He responded by flying home to Aberdeen, knowing that Torino would not get a penny in transfer fees if he refused to play at Juventus.<sup id="cite_ref-book_4-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> He eventually signed for United on 10 July 1962, for a new British record fee of £115,000.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;note 3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-book_4-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-torcar_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-torcar-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although his time in Italy was mixed, Law was voted number one foreign player in Italy ahead of teammate Joe Baker, <a href="/wiki/Fiorentina" class="mw-redirect" title="Fiorentina">Fiorentina</a> winger <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Hamrin" title="Kurt Hamrin">Kurt Hamrin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Inter Milan</a> midfielder <a href="/wiki/Luis_Su%C3%A1rez_Miramontes" class="mw-redirect" title="Luis Suárez Miramontes">Luis Suarez</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tor_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tor-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>  The lifestyle and culture of a foreign country was an eye-opener for the young Scotsman, and the medical expertise and sports science in Italy was far ahead of what was available in the UK at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-tor_17-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tor-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>  Ultimately though, Law found the football to be joyless and overly defensive, with him being subjected to violent man marking and heavy tackling on a frequent basis.<sup id="cite_ref-tor_17-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tor-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manchester_United">Manchester United</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denis_Law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Manchester United">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Glory_years">Glory years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denis_Law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Glory years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dennis_law_statue.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Dennis_law_statue.jpg/220px-Dennis_law_statue.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Dennis_law_statue.jpg/330px-Dennis_law_statue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Dennis_law_statue.jpg/440px-Dennis_law_statue.jpg 2x" data-file-width="459" data-file-height="418" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dennis_law_statue.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Law as depicted on a statue at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a> which honours him, <a href="/wiki/George_Best" title="George Best">George Best</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Charlton" title="Bobby Charlton">Bobby Charlton</a> as the "<b><a href="/wiki/United_Trinity" title="United Trinity">United Trinity</a></b>"</div></div></div>
<p>Law moved back to <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>, boarding with the same landlady with whom he had lived during his time as a City player. His first match for United was against <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Bromwich Albion</a> on 18 August 1962, and he made an excellent start, scoring after only seven minutes. The match finished in a 2–2 draw. However, United's form had been erratic since the <a href="/wiki/Munich_air_disaster" title="Munich air disaster">Munich air disaster</a> in 1958, and because of their inconsistency they spent the season fighting relegation. In a league match against <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a> Law scored a <a href="/wiki/Hat_trick" class="mw-redirect" title="Hat trick">hat trick</a> but United still lost. They found form in the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> though, with Law scoring another hat trick in a 5–0 win against his old club Huddersfield Town, and they went on to reach the final against Leicester City. Leicester were strong favourites, having finished fourth in the league, but Law scored the first goal as United won 3–1 in what turned out to be the only FA Cup final of his career.<sup id="cite_ref-facup63_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facup63-23">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> He also married his wife Diana that season, on 11 December 1962.
</p><p>An incident took place that season that Law felt had repercussions in later years. In a match against West Brom on 15 December 1962, the referee Gilbert Pullin consistently goaded Law with taunts such as "Oh, you clever so and so, you can't play", and after the match, Law and his manager <a href="/wiki/Matt_Busby" title="Matt Busby">Matt Busby</a> reported the matter to <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">the Football Association</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> A disciplinary committee decided that Pullin should be severely censured, but he did not accept their verdict and quit the game. Law later claimed that "in the eyes of some referees, I was a marked man" and blamed the incident for the "staggeringly heavy punishments" that he received later in his career.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Law scored a number of goals early in the <a href="/wiki/1963%E2%80%9364_in_English_football" title="1963–64 in English football">1963–64 season</a> and was selected to play for a <i>Rest of the World</i> side against <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley</a>, scoring their goal in a 2–1 defeat.<sup id="cite_ref-fifa_xi_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fifa_xi-26">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> He later described this as the greatest honour of his career.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> His season was interrupted by a 28-day suspension for a sending off that he received against <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a>. The unusually cold winter forced United to play many of their fixtures in a short time, and their results suffered. Law later blamed this for United's failure to win a trophy in that season. Despite the lack of silverware, Law enjoyed a prolific goalscoring season and finished the campaign with 46 goals in all competitions, still a club record today.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/1964%E2%80%9365_in_English_football" title="1964–65 in English football">1964–65</a>, Law won the <a href="/wiki/Ballon_d%27Or_(1956%E2%80%932009)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ballon d&#39;Or (1956–2009)">Ballon d'Or</a> award,<sup id="cite_ref-bdor_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bdor-29">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> and Manchester United won their first league title since Munich.<sup id="cite_ref-11v11_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11v11-30">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Law's 28 league goals that season made him the First Division's top scorer.
</p><p>The following season, Law injured his right knee while playing for Scotland against <a href="/wiki/Poland_national_football_team" title="Poland national football team">Poland</a> on 21 October 1965. He had previously had an operation on the same knee while at Huddersfield,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> and the injury was to trouble him for the rest of his career.
</p><p>In 1966, Law asked United's manager Matt Busby to give him a pay rise at his next contract renewal, and threatened to leave the club if he did not get one. Busby immediately placed Law on the transfer list, announcing that "no player will hold this club to ransom, no player". When Law went to see him, Busby pulled out a written apology for him to sign, showing it to the press once he had done so.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Law later claimed that Busby had used the incident to warn other players not to do the same thing, but had secretly given him the pay rise.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>  Despite all this, Law scored 23 goals in 36 league appearances during <a href="/wiki/1966%E2%80%9367_in_English_football" title="1966–67 in English football">1966–67</a>, helping United win the league title again.<sup id="cite_ref-11v11_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11v11-30">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mustats_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mustats-34">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1968, United won the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">European Cup</a> for the first time, but Law's knee injury was causing him serious problems and he missed both the semi-final and the <a href="/wiki/1968_European_Cup_Final" title="1968 European Cup Final">final</a> as a result. He was regularly given <a href="/wiki/Corticosteroid" title="Corticosteroid">cortisone</a> injections to ease the pain, but playing while the knee was still injured was causing long-term damage. He visited a specialist in January 1968 who wrote to United claiming that a previous operation to remove the cartilage from the knee had failed and recommending that a second operation be performed, but Law was not shown the report for several years and had to continue full training.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/1968%E2%80%9369_in_English_football" title="1968–69 in English football">1968–69</a>, United reached the semi-final of the European Cup, playing <a href="/wiki/AC_Milan" class="mw-redirect" title="AC Milan">AC Milan</a>. United lost the first leg in the San Siro 2–0, winning the <a href="/wiki/Two-legged_match" class="mw-redirect" title="Two-legged match">second leg</a> at Old Trafford 1–0 with a Bobby Charlton goal. Having scored seven times in the 10–2 aggregate first round victory over <a href="/wiki/Waterford_United_F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Waterford United F.C.">Waterford United</a>, Law finished as top scorer in the tournament with 9 goals.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Decline">Decline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denis_Law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Decline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Wilf_McGuinness" title="Wilf McGuinness">Wilf McGuinness</a> took over as first team coach at the start of the <a href="/wiki/1969%E2%80%9370_in_English_football" title="1969–70 in English football">1969–70 season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> United finished eighth in the league, but Law missed almost all of the season through injury, and in April 1970 he was transfer listed for £60,000. Nobody made a bid for him, so he stayed at United.<sup id="cite_ref-espns_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-espns-37">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After a poor <a href="/wiki/1970%E2%80%9371_in_English_football" title="1970–71 in English football">1970–71 season</a>, United appointed <a href="/wiki/Frank_O%27Farrell" title="Frank O&#39;Farrell">Frank O'Farrell</a> as manager. They made a good start to the <a href="/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_in_English_football" title="1971–72 in English football">1971–72 season</a> and finished 1971 five points clear at the top of the league, with Law having scored twelve goals. However, results deteriorated and they finished the season in eighth place.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Law scored in the first match of the following season, <a href="/wiki/1972%E2%80%9373_in_English_football" title="1972–73 in English football">1972–73</a>, but his knee injury was troubling him again, and he failed to score for the rest of the season. The poor results continued and O'Farrell was sacked.
</p><p>Law recommended that United replace O'Farrell with <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Docherty" title="Tommy Docherty">Tommy Docherty</a>, whom he knew from his time playing with the Scottish national side.<sup id="cite_ref-espns_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-espns-37">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The club followed his recommendation, and things started well, with the team's improved results lifting them into mid-table.<sup id="cite_ref-espns_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-espns-37">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_Manchester_City">Return to Manchester City</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denis_Law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Return to Manchester City">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Law was given a free transfer by Tommy Docherty in the summer of 1973,<sup id="cite_ref-espns_37-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-espns-37">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> after 11 years at the club during which he had scored a total of 237 goals in 404 games in all competitions, as well as collecting two league title medals and an FA Cup winner's medal. Only <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Charlton" title="Bobby Charlton">Bobby Charlton</a> (who retired in 1973) and <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Rooney" title="Wayne Rooney">Wayne Rooney</a> have scored more goals for United.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Law was then offered a contract by Manchester City manager <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Hart_(footballer)" title="Johnny Hart (footballer)">Johnny Hart</a>, scoring two goals on his debut against <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_City_F.C." title="Birmingham City F.C.">Birmingham City</a> in the opening game of the season 1973–74.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> He made 27 full appearances and two as substitute in that season, including City's 2–1 defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Cup">League Cup</a> final against <a href="/wiki/Wolverhampton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Wolverhampton Wanderers F.C.">Wolves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> In City's last game of the <a href="/wiki/1973%E2%80%9374_in_English_football" title="1973–74 in English football">1973–74 season</a> against Manchester United at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a>, Law's 81st-minute back-heeled goal gave City a 1–0 lead but, thinking his goal might relegate United, Law <a href="/wiki/Goal_celebration#Notable_non-celebrations" title="Goal celebration">did not celebrate the goal</a>. Results of the day's other matches meant that United were relegated whatever their result, but Law did not know that at the time. A number of pitch invasions by United fans followed, and Law walked off the pitch with his head down as he was substituted. The pitch invasions forced the referee to abandon the game in the 85th minute. After a review, the <a href="/wiki/Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League">Football League</a> decided that the result should stand.<sup id="cite_ref-espns_37-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-espns-37">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Law still had a contract with Manchester City, but new manager <a href="/wiki/Tony_Book" title="Tony Book">Tony Book</a> told him that he would only be playing reserve team football if he stayed at the club in the new season. He did not want to end his career in this way, so he retired from professional football in the summer of 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Law played two games for Manchester City in the season 1974–75, in the pre-season <a href="/wiki/Texaco_Cup" title="Texaco Cup">Texaco Cup</a> tournament, scoring the last goal of his career in the game against <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United_F.C." title="Sheffield United F.C.">Sheffield United</a> at <a href="/wiki/Bramall_Lane" title="Bramall Lane">Bramall Lane</a> on 6 August 1974. His last professional game was the 2–1 victory against <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Athletic_A.F.C." title="Oldham Athletic A.F.C.">Oldham Athletic</a> at <a href="/wiki/Maine_Road" title="Maine Road">Maine Road</a> on 10 August 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> He formally retired on 26 August 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denis_Law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Law was not chosen to play for Scotland in the <a href="/wiki/1958_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1958 FIFA World Cup">1958 FIFA World Cup</a>, but was given his debut in a <a href="/wiki/British_Home_Championship" title="British Home Championship">British Home Championship</a> match against <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_football_team" title="Wales national football team">Wales</a> on 18 October 1958 by <a href="/wiki/Matt_Busby" title="Matt Busby">Matt Busby</a>, who managed Scotland on a temporary basis for two matches. Law scored Scotland's second goal in a 3–0 win over the Welsh at <a href="/wiki/Ninian_Park" title="Ninian Park">Ninian Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> He played but did not score in Scotland's match against <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> on 15 April 1961. Scotland lost the match 9–3, and Law described it as his "blackest day".<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> While with Torino, Law continued to play for Scotland, although the club were not keen to release him for international matches and had put a clause into his contract stating that they were not obliged to do so.
</p><p>Law was chosen for the Rest of the World team that faced England in the FA Centenary match in 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-fifa_xi_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fifa_xi-26">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Law injured his right knee while playing for Scotland against <a href="/wiki/Poland_national_football_team" title="Poland national football team">Poland</a> on 21 October 1965. Law scored in Scotland's famous 3–2 victory over England on 15 April 1967 in the <a href="/wiki/1967_British_Home_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="1967 British Home Championship">1967 British Home Championship</a>, less than a year after England had become world champions. Manchester United won the league that season, but Law felt that the victory over England was even more satisfying.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Scotland reached the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a> finals in the summer of <a href="/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1974 FIFA World Cup">1974</a>, for the first time since 1958. Although he had not played much first team football in the preceding season, Law was included in the squad and played in their first match, against <a href="/wiki/Zaire_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Zaire national football team">Zaire</a>. He didn't score, but Scotland won 2–0. Law was "very disappointed" not to be picked for the following match against <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazil</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> and was not selected for the following match against <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia_national_football_team" title="Yugoslavia national football team">Yugoslavia</a> either. Although Scotland were not defeated in any of their matches, they did not qualify for the second phase and were out of the World Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The match against Zaire proved to be the last of Law's 55 appearances for Scotland.
</p><p>Law jointly holds the Scottish international record goal tally with 30 goals.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;note 4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denis_Law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>He first met his wife-to-be, Diana, in an <a href="/wiki/Aberdeenshire" title="Aberdeenshire">Aberdeenshire</a> dancehall when they were both still teenagers.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> They married in December 1962 and went on to have five children.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Their daughter, also called Diana, worked for several years in the Manchester United press office.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Their other children are Gary, Andrew, Robert and Iain. They also have five grandchildren, Emilia, Isla, Ollie, James and Harvey. Denis and Diana still live in the <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> area.
</p><p>Since retiring as a player, Law has often worked on <a href="/wiki/Radio" title="Radio">radio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Television" title="Television">television</a> summarising and presenting games. Denis was one of the first sport news presenters of <a href="/wiki/Granada_Reports" title="Granada Reports">Granada Reports</a> and was the sub-presenter of <a href="/wiki/Granada_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Granada Television">Granada Television</a>'s Match Time, the equivalent of <a href="/wiki/LWT" class="mw-redirect" title="LWT">LWT</a>'s <a href="/wiki/The_Big_Match" title="The Big Match">The Big Match</a>. He appeared as a special guest on the TV guest show <i><a href="/wiki/This_Is_Your_Life_(UK_TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="This Is Your Life (UK TV series)">This Is Your Life</a></i> on 19 February 1975, months after retiring as a player.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Denis_Law_-_%22Legend%22_(geograph_3143626).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Denis_Law_-_%22Legend%22_%28geograph_3143626%29.jpg/220px-Denis_Law_-_%22Legend%22_%28geograph_3143626%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Denis_Law_-_%22Legend%22_%28geograph_3143626%29.jpg/330px-Denis_Law_-_%22Legend%22_%28geograph_3143626%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Denis_Law_-_%22Legend%22_%28geograph_3143626%29.jpg/440px-Denis_Law_-_%22Legend%22_%28geograph_3143626%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3216" data-file-height="4288" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Denis_Law_-_%22Legend%22_(geograph_3143626).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>statue to Law in <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen" title="Aberdeen">Aberdeen</a></div></div></div>
<p>Law was made an Inaugural Inductee of the <a href="/wiki/English_Football_Hall_of_Fame" title="English Football Hall of Fame">English Football Hall of Fame</a> in 2002 in recognition of his impact on the English game. On 23 February 2002, a statue of Law (alongside George Best and Bobby Charlton) was unveiled at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a>, in the part of the stadium known as the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Scoreboard_End&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Scoreboard End (page does not exist)">Scoreboard End</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> He had a successful operation to treat <a href="/wiki/Prostate_cancer" title="Prostate cancer">prostate cancer</a> in November 2003<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> and was awarded honorary degrees from the Universities of <a href="/wiki/University_of_Aberdeen" title="University of Aberdeen">Aberdeen</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_St._Andrews" class="mw-redirect" title="University of St. Andrews">St. Andrews</a> in 2005,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Gordon_University" title="Robert Gordon University">Robert Gordon University</a> in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The emergence of <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Dutch</a> international <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Bergkamp" title="Dennis Bergkamp">Dennis Bergkamp</a> in the 1990s uncovered a story that the player's parents were fans of Law and named their son after him.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> However, Dutch authorities refused to recognise the name unless it was spelt with two <i>n</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s as they felt it was otherwise too similar to the female name <i>Denise</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 25 November 2005, Law was at the bedside of former United teammate <a href="/wiki/George_Best" title="George Best">George Best</a> as he died of multiple organ failure.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2008, at the City of Manchester Stadium, Law (with UEFA president <a href="/wiki/Michel_Platini" title="Michel Platini">Michel Platini</a>) presented the medals to the winners of the UEFA Cup, <a href="/wiki/FC_Zenit_Saint_Petersburg" title="FC Zenit Saint Petersburg">Zenit Saint Petersburg</a> and their opponents, Scottish side <a href="/wiki/Rangers_F.C." title="Rangers F.C.">Rangers</a>.
</p><p>In February 2010, Law was named as patron of the UK based charity Football Aid, taking over from the late <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Robson" title="Bobby Robson">Sir Bobby Robson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, a statue to Law, commissioned by the <i>Denis Law Legacy Trust</i>, was unveiled at the entrance to <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_University_Sports_Union#Aberdeen_Sports_Village" title="Aberdeen University Sports Union">Aberdeen Sports Village</a> (a facility he had formally opened two years earlier) depicting his pose after scoring for Scotland against England in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Law was appointed <a href="/wiki/Commander_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander of the Order of the British Empire">Commander of the Order of the British Empire</a> (CBE) in the <a href="/wiki/2016_New_Year_Honours" title="2016 New Year Honours">2016 New Year Honours</a> for services to football and charity.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, Law received the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_City_of_Aberdeen" title="Freedom of the City of Aberdeen">Freedom of the City of Aberdeen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_statistics">Career statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denis_Law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Career statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_appearances">International appearances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denis_Law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: International appearances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denis_Law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_2">Club</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denis_Law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Club">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<dl><dt>Manchester United</dt></dl>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Football_League_First_Division" title="Football League First Division">Football League First Division</a>: <a href="/wiki/1964%E2%80%9365_Football_League" title="1964–65 Football League">1964–65</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-11v11_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11v11-30">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/1966%E2%80%9367_Football_League" title="1966–67 Football League">1966–67</a><sup id="cite_ref-11v11_30-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11v11-30">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a>: <a href="/wiki/1963_FA_Cup_Final" title="1963 FA Cup Final">1962–63</a><sup id="cite_ref-facup63_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facup63-23">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/FA_Community_Shield" title="FA Community Shield">Charity Shield</a>: <a href="/wiki/1965_FA_Charity_Shield" title="1965 FA Charity Shield">1965</a>, <a href="/wiki/1967_FA_Charity_Shield" title="1967 FA Charity Shield">1967</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">European Cup</a>: <a href="/wiki/1968_European_Cup_Final" title="1968 European Cup Final">1967–68</a></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Individual">Individual</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Denis_Law&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Individual">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ballon_d%27Or_(1956%E2%80%932009)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ballon d&#39;Or (1956–2009)">Ballon d'Or</a>: <a href="/wiki/1964_Ballon_d%27Or" title="1964 Ballon d&#39;Or">1964</a><sup id="cite_ref-bdor_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bdor-29">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/World_Soccer_(magazine)" title="World Soccer (magazine)">World Soccer</a> World XI: 1964<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_European_Cup_and_UEFA_Champions_League_top_scorers" title="List of European Cup and UEFA Champions League top scorers">European Cup top scorer</a>: <a href="/wiki/1968%E2%80%9369_European_Cup" title="1968–69 European Cup">1968–69</a><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Football_League_100_Legends" title="Football League 100 Legends">Football League 100 Legends</a>: 1974<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/PFA_Merit_Award" title="PFA Merit Award">PFA Merit Award</a>: 1975<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team_roll_of_honour" class="mw-redirect" title="Scotland national football team roll of honour">Scotland national football team roll of honour</a> (players with 50+ caps): inducted in 1988<sup id="cite_ref-sroh_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sroh-79">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/FWA_Tribute_Award" title="FWA Tribute Award">FWA Tribute Award</a>: 1994<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Inaugural Inductee of the <a href="/wiki/English_Football_Hall_of_Fame" title="English Football Hall of Fame">English Football Hall of Fame</a>: 2002<sup id="cite_ref-hof_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hof-81">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Scotland's <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Jubilee_Awards" title="UEFA Jubilee Awards">Golden Player</a>: Most Outstanding Player of the past 50 years by the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Football_Association" title="Scottish Football Association">Scottish Football Association</a> (November 2003, to celebrate <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Jubilee_Awards" title="UEFA Jubilee Awards">UEFA's Jubilee</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scottish_Football_Hall_of_Fame" title="Scottish Football Hall of Fame">Scottish Football Hall of Fame</a>: inducted in 2004<sup id="cite_ref-shof_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shof-83">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Professional_Footballers%27_Association" title="Professional Footballers&#39; Association">PFA</a> Team of the Century (1907-1976): 2007<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
